Reduction of Kharaj When Land Cannot Bear It
Ruling on adjusting kharaj based on land's capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for reducing kharaj and explain the Hanafi prohibition on increasing it, distinguishing between the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Kharaj must not exceed half the produce; reduction is wajib when land cannot bear, increase is never allowed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on adjusting kharaj when land cannot bear the assessment. The text from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the condition for reduction and the prohibition of increase, supported by the practice of Caliph Umar. We will explore the proofs, the disagreement with al-Shafi'i, and the intra-Hanafi difference on whether an initial assessment can be set higher than Umar's benchmark.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: if the land cannot bear the assessed kharaj (wazifa), the assessment is reduced. Conversely, increase is prohibited. Determine the hukm level—reduction is wajib when the condition is met; increase is haram.
The condition for inability is that the produce is less than double the kharaj (i.e., kharaj > half the produce).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Umar (ra). He asked his tax collectors, Uthman ibn Hunayf and Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, whether they had burdened the land beyond its capacity. Their response and Umar's acceptance imply that reduction would have been required if they had overburdened it.
This is a qawl sahabi (statement of a companion) and is considered a strong precedent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's question presupposes that overburdening is wrong and must be corrected. The fact that he did not increase the assessment when informed of capacity shows that increase is not part of the sunna. The limit of half the produce is derived from Umar's established practice.
The exact wording 'if we increased, it would bear it' shows the land had capacity, yet Umar did not increase.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i rejects reduction, arguing the assessment is fixed. Within Hanafi school, Muhammad al-Shaybani permits initial increase by analogy to reduction, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf forbid it. The author sides with Abu Yusuf.
The consensus on forbidding increase after assessment is noted; the dispute is only about initial setting.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author (al-Karkhi or al-Marghinani) chooses the view of Abu Yusuf, making the mufta bihi: no increase at any stage, and reduction only when produce does not reach double the assessed kharaj.
The maximum assessment is half the produce, as per Umar's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم تطق ما وظف نقص، بخلاف الزيادة. أي وإن لم تطق الأرض ما وظف مما ذكرنا على كل جريب من أقسام الزراعة تنقص الوظيفة إلى ما تطيق، ومعنى عدم الإطاقة أن الخارج منها لا يبلغ ضعف الخراج الموظف فينقض منه إلى نصف الخراج، والحاصل أن النقصان عند قلة الربع جائز ؛ لقول عمر الهلهلهلهله لعثمان بن حنيف وحذيفة بن اليمان ما: لعلكما حملتماها ما لا تطيق فقالا: لا بل حملناها ما تطيق ولو زدنا لأطاقت وهذا دليل جواز النقصان، وبه قال مالك وأحمد خلافاً للشافعي، بخلاف الزيادة أي وإن كانت تطيق الأرض الزيادة على الوظيفة التي صدرت عمر رضي انه بأن كثر ربعها فإنها لا تجوز إجماعاً. عند وأما إذا أراد الإمام توظيف الخراج على أرض تطيق الزيادة ابتداء وزاد على وظيفة عمر له فإنها لا تجوز أيضاً . أبي حنيفة وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف وهو رواية عن أحمد؛ لأن عمر الله لم يزد لما أخبر بزيادة الطاقة، وقال محمد: يجوز اعتباراً للزيادة بالنقصان وبه قالت الثلاثة، واختار المصنف قول أبي يوسف ثم نهاية الطاقة نصف الخارج ولا يزاد عليه [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٦/١] (مستخلص، فتح)
And if [the land] cannot bear what was assessed, it is reduced, contrary to increase. That is: if the land cannot bear what was assessed for each jarib of the types of cultivation, the assessment is reduced to what it can bear. The meaning of inability is that the produce does not reach double the assessed kharaj, so it is reduced to half the kharaj. The summary is that reduction when the produce is low is permissible because of the statement of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) to Uthman ibn Hunayf and Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman: 'Perhaps you have burdened it with what it cannot bear.' They said: 'No, we have burdened it with what it can bear, and if we increased it would bear it.' This is evidence for the permissibility of reduction. And Malik and Ahmad said this, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Contrary to increase, that is: if the land can bear an increase over the assessment that came from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) because its produce is abundant, it is not permissible by consensus. And if the imam wants to assess kharaj on land that can bear an increase from the beginning and increases over Umar's assessment, it is also not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf and a narration from Ahmad, because Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) did not increase when informed of increased capacity. Muhammad said: it is permissible, considering increase by analogy to reduction, and the three (schools) said this. The author chose the view of Abu Yusuf, then the limit of capacity is half of the produce and nothing more is added.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on adjusting kharaj (land tax) assessments. The matn states that if the land cannot bear the assessed amount, it is reduced; increase is prohibited. The commentary explains that 'cannot bear' means the produce is less than double the kharaj (i.e., kharaj exceeds half the produce), so the kharaj is halved. The proof is from the practice of Caliph Umar, who questioned his tax collectors and accepted their assurance that the assessment was within capacity, implying that reduction would have been permissible if it were not. This establishes the permissibility of reduction. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the assessment is fixed. The increase is prohibited by consensus, both retroactively and initially (when the imam sets a new assessment). Within the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in one narration) disallow any increase beyond Umar's scale, while Muhammad al-Shaybani permits it by analogy to reduction. The author favors Abu Yusuf's view. The maximum assessment is half of the produce.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land, typically a fixed amount per unit area, assessed by the imam.
وظيفة (wazifa): The assessed amount of kharaj imposed on each unit of land (e.g., per jarib).
إطاقة (itaqa): The capacity of the land to bear the kharaj, measured by whether the produce is at least double the assessed amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition under which the kharaj assessment is reduced for a piece of land?
A) The landowner requests a reduction
B) The produce from the land is less than double the assessed kharaj
C) The landowner converts to Islam
D) The land is bought by a Muslim

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, kharaj must be adjusted so that it does not exceed half the produce; reduction is required when produce is insufficient, and increase is never allowed.

Exemption from Kharaj Due to Natural Disasters
Ruling with proof on kharaj exemption due to natural calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for kharaj exemption due to natural calamities and apply the proportional reduction rule.

Core Idea
Natural calamities that destroy the crop waive kharaj; preventable damage does not.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains when a landowner is exempt from paying kharaj (land tax) due to natural disasters. It distinguishes between unpreventable calamities like floods, hail, and locusts, which cancel the tax, and preventable losses such as animal attacks, which do not. The ruling relies on the principle that kharaj is based on the land's growth potential throughout the year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exempting scenarios
The passage lists three situations where kharaj is not due: when water overwhelms the land past planting time; when water is cut off and cultivation is impossible; or when a celestial calamity destroys the crop entirely.
2
Understand the rationale: loss of growth potential
The exemption is based on the loss of the land's estimated growth potential (namā' taqdīrī), which is considered throughout the tax year. Without the ability to cultivate, the basis for kharaj is absent.
This is analogous to zakat, where continuous growth is a condition.
3
Restrict exemption to unpreventable calamities
Only calamities that are heavenly and cannot be guarded against (e.g., locusts, hail, flood, fire) qualify. Preventable damages like attacks by monkeys or livestock do not exempt.
The text explicitly uses 'āfah samāwiyyah' (celestial calamity).
4
Apply the proportional rule for partial loss
If the entire produce is lost, no kharaj is due. If only part is lost, check the remaining produce: if it covers the kharaj amount plus an equal surplus, full kharaj is due; if less, then half the kharaj is due (as a fair measure).
The condition is that the remaining produce must be at least double the kharaj to be fully liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن غلب إلخ أي غلب الماء على أرض الخراج حتى مضى وقت الزراعة، أو انقطع الماء عنها ولم يتمكن صاحبها من الزراعة، أو أصاب الزرع آفة لا يمكن دفعها كالجراد والبرد والغرق والحرق، فلا خراج على صاحب الأرض؛ لأنه فات التمكن من الزراعة، وهو النماء التقديري المعتبر في باب الخراج في غلبة الماء والانقطاع، وفيما أصاب الزرع آفة، فات النماء في بعض الحول، وكونه نامياً في جميع الحول شرط كما في مال الزكاة، وقيدنا الآفة بالسماوية التي لا يمكن الاحتراز عنها؛ لأن في آفة يمكن دفعها والاحتراز عنها كأكل القردة والسباع والأنعام، لا يسقط الخراج والمراد بإصابة الآفة أن يذهب كل الخارج، فلا خراج في هذه الصورة؛ لأن الأصل إذا هلك بطل ما تعلق به. السنة أما إذا ذهب بعضه فإن بقي مقدار الخراج ومثله بأن بقي مقدار درهمين وقفيزين يجب الخراج؛ لأنه لا يزيد على نصف الخارج، وإن بقي أقل من ذلك، يجب نصفه؛ لأن التنصيف عين الإنصاف. وقيد بالزرع؛ لأنه لو ملك بعد الحصاد لا يسقط، وقيل: عدم الخراج في صورة هلاك الخارج محمول على ما إذا لم يبق من مقدار ما يمكنه أن يزرع الأرض ثانياً، وأما إذا بقي من المدة قدر ذلك، فلا يسقط. (عيني) أو انقطع الماء عنها لعدم التمكن من الزراعة كالأرض السنجة التي لا تنبت شيئا. (عيني)
If it is overwhelmed etc.: i.e., if water overwhelms the kharaj land until the planting time has passed, or water is cut off from it and its owner cannot cultivate, or a calamity strikes the crop that cannot be repelled, like locusts, hail, drowning, or fire, then there is no kharaj on the owner of the land because the ability to cultivate is lost, which is the estimated growth considered in the subject of kharaj in cases of water overwhelm and cutoff, and in the case of a crop calamity, growth is lost for part of the year. And being productive throughout the year is a condition, as in zakat money. We have restricted the calamity to a celestial one that cannot be guarded against, because in a calamity that can be repelled and guarded against, like eating by monkeys, predatory animals, and livestock, the kharaj is not remitted. The meaning of 'crop struck by calamity' is that all of the produce is lost, so there is no kharaj in this case because when the principal is destroyed, what depends on it is void. As for if part of it is lost, then if there remains the amount of the kharaj and the like of it (i.e., there remains two dirhams and two qafiz), the kharaj is obligatory because it does not exceed half the produce; if less than that remains, half of it is obligatory because half is the fair measure. And it is restricted to the crop because if he takes possession after harvest, it is not remitted. And it is said that the absence of kharaj in the case of destruction of produce is carried on the condition that there does not remain enough time for him to cultivate the land a second time; if there remains enough time, it is not remitted. (Ayni) Or water is cut off from it due to inability to cultivate, like the stony land that does not grow anything. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on exemption from kharaj when natural disasters prevent cultivation. The matn states three scenarios: water overwhelms land, water cuts off, or a crop calamity occurs. The commentary explains that in all cases, the owner is not liable for kharaj because the land's potential for growth (the basis for kharaj) is lost. The condition is that the calamity must be from heaven (natural) and unpreventable; preventable calamities like animal attacks do not waive kharaj. If the entire produce is lost, no kharaj is due. If only part is lost, the calculation depends on remaining produce: if enough remains to cover the kharaj plus an equal amount (i.e., double the kharaj), then the full kharaj is due; if less, then only half the kharaj is due, because half is the fair measure. This is analogous to zakat money where growth throughout the year is required.

Key Terms
آفة سماوية (āfah samāwiyyah): A calamity from the sky (natural disaster) that cannot be prevented, such as locusts, hail, flood, or fire.
نماء تقديري (namā’ taqdīrī): Estimated growth potential of land, which is the basis for kharaj assessment throughout the year.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land in Islamic states.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a farmer's crop is completely eaten by wild animals, is the kharaj waived?
A) Yes, because the crop is destroyed
B) No, because this is a preventable calamity
C) Yes, if the animals are from the wilderness
D) No, because animals are not a celestial calamity

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is exempted only when natural, unpreventable calamities destroy the crop or prevent cultivation; partial loss leads to proportional reduction.

Churches, Dress, and Distinction: Hanafi Rulings on Dhimmis
Rulings on churches and dhimmi distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rebuilding collapsed churches and the requirements for dhimmis to be distinguished in dress and riding, and evaluate the Hanbali opposition.

Core Idea
Dhimmis maintain old churches but may not build new ones; they must be visibly distinct from Muslims in dress, mount, and by wearing the kastij.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two key aspects of the dhimmi contract: the maintenance of their places of worship and the requirement to be visually distinct from Muslims. These rulings aim to preserve the honor of Islam while allowing dhimmis to practice their religion, but with clear social boundaries that reflect the hierarchical relationship between Muslims and non-Muslims in a Muslim polity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Main Rulings
Read the passage carefully: first, churches and synagogues that collapse naturally may be rebuilt without increase; second, dhimmis must be distinguished from Muslims in dress, mount, saddle, and by wearing a thick belt called kastij. Mark these two distinctly.
The passage also discusses the striking of bells and the prohibition of building new places of worship in certain areas.
2
Analyze the Ruling on Rebuilding Churches
Focus on the Hanafi position: an old church that falls down on its own may be rebuilt to its original dimensions, but not if the imam demolished it. Note the Hanbali opposition and the distinction between cities, villages, and the Arabian Peninsula.
The Hanafi proof is continuous practice (tawaruth) from the Prophet's time.
3
Analyze the Ruling on Distinguishing Dhimmis
List the required distinctions: clothing (no scholarly or noble attire), mount (no horses, donkeys with pack-saddles), saddles (no expensive saddles), and the kastij belt. Understand the historical justification: 'Umar's order with Companion consensus.
The objection that the Prophet didn't impose such distinctions is answered by the change in circumstances.
4
Examine the Dalil and Madhhab Dispute
Identify the hadith cited for the Arabian Peninsula: 'Expel the polytheists.' Note that Ahmad ibn Hanbal extends the prohibition to rebuilding, while Hanafis allow it based on practice. Evaluate the strength of each proof.
The Hanafi emphasis on 'amal (practice) as a source of law is evident here.
5
Apply the Rulings to a Hypothetical Scenario
Consider a dhimmi community in a village outside Arabia: their church collapses naturally. Determine the Hanafi ruling (rebuild as before) and what restrictions apply. Then, if a dhimmi wants to ride a horse, what must he do? (He may not, unless out of necessity, and must use a pack-saddle.)
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) with Hanbalis: they would not allow rebuilding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير والجهاد

أحكام الجزية

وكنيسة في دارنا، ويعاد المنهدم. ويميّز الذمّيُّ عنا في الزي والمركب والسرج، أي عن المسلمين أي وفي المركب لأنهم من أهل الإهانة من هي كثير .

وضرب الناقوس خارج الكنيسة، والناقوس لهم كالأذان لنا، فيقطع به إظهار الشرك، وقوله: "في دارنا" أي في دار الإسلام مطلقا لا في الأمصار ، ولا في القرى.(مستخلص، فتح، عيني) في دارنا: أي في دار الإسلام أي لا تبنيان ابتداء إن لم يكونا فيها (محشي) ويعاد المنهدم: [ أي ما انهدم بنفسه الكنائس والبيع القديمة لا ما هدمه الإمام، ويعاد من غير زيادة على البناء الأول (عيني)] أي لو الهدمت البيع والكنائس القديمة لا يمنع من إعادتها؛ لأن التوارث من لدن رسول الله له إلى يومنا هذا بترك البيع والكنائس في دار الإسلام، فهذا دليل جواز الإعادة؛ لأن البيعة لا تبقي دائمة إلا أنه يمنع من الزيادة على البناء الأول، وعند أحمد: لا يعاد المنهدم أيضاً، وقيل: هذا في الأمصار دون القرى في غير جزيرة العرب، أما فيها فيمنعون من قراها أيضاً لخبر "لا يجتمع دينان في جزيرة العرب" ويمنعون في الأمصار؛ لأنها التي تقام فيها شعائر الإسلام ولا يمنعون من ذلك في قرية لا يقام فيها الجمع والحدود وإن كان فيها عدد وقيل: يمنعون في كل موضع لم تشع فيه شعائرهم، والمروي عن أبي حنيفة كان في قرى الكوفة؛ لأن أكثر أهلها أهل الذمة، وفي أرض العرب يمنعون من ذلك كله، ومن إدخال الخمر والخنازير فيها، ويمنعون من المشركين مسكناً؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه عليه قال في مرضه الذي مات فيه: "أخرجوا المشركين من جزيرة العرب"، رواه البخاري ومسلم رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٩/١] (فتح) ويميز الذمّي عنا في الزّي: قال النووي في شرح مسلم": الزي بفتح الزاء وكسرها وتشديد الياء، الهيئة واللباس أي يؤخذ الذمّي بالتميز عن معشر المسلمين في اللباس والكسوة، ويمنعون عن لباس يختص بأهل العلم والشرف، وكذا يؤاخذون في المركب بأن يمنعوا من ركوب الخيل، وكذا في السروج بأن يركبوا سرجاً كهيئة الأكف إذا ركبوا حماراً أو بغلاً، أو ركبوا خيلاً للضرورة، وكذا يمنعون عن استعمال السلاح، ويؤخذ بإظهار الكستيج بضم ا الكاف وسكون السين المهملة وكسر التاء الفوقية.

اتخاذها

فإن قيل: لم يأخذ النبي عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام يهود المدينة ولا نصارى نجران ولا مجوس هجر بذلك فكيف يؤخذ الذمي بهذه؟ قلنا: إنهم في زمن رسول الله له كانوا معروفين في المدينة لا يشتبه حالهم فلم يقع الاحتياج إلى ذلك ثم في زمن عمر الله لما كثر في الناس من يعرف ومن لا يعرف وقعت الحاجة إلى ذلك، فأمر بذلك بمحضر من الصحابة وكانوا يرونه صوابا ولأنهم من أهل الإهانة والمسلمون من أهل الإعزاز والكرامة فوجب التميز إظهاراً للتفاوت بينهما، و"الكستيج" الخيط الغليظ الذي يشدون به أوساطهم، وعن أبي يوسف هو الخيط الغليظ بقدر الإصبع يشدّه الذمي فوق ثيابه دون ما يتميز به من الزنانير المتخذة عن الإبريسم، وقال فخر الإسلام الكستيجات هي علامات الكفر، وهي فارسية معربة وحقيقته العجز والذل بلغة العجم.
The Book of Siyar and Jihad. Rulings of Jizyah. And a church in our territory, and the demolished one is rebuilt. And the dhimmi is distinguished from us in dress, mount, and saddle. Striking the bell outside the church, and the bell for them is like the adhan for us, thus it cuts the display of shirk. And his saying 'in our territory' means in the land of Islam absolutely, not in cities and not in villages. The demolished: meaning what collapsed by itself of old churches and synagogues, not what the imam demolished, and it is rebuilt without increase over the original building. ... And the dhimmi is distinguished from us in dress: An-Nawawi said in Sharh Muslim: az-zay (dress) means appearance and clothing, i.e., the dhimmi is required to be distinguished from Muslims in clothing and garments, and they are prevented from wearing clothes specific to scholars and nobility. Similarly, they are restricted in mount by being prevented from riding horses, and in saddles by riding a saddle like a pack-saddle when riding a donkey or mule, or riding a horse out of necessity. They are also prevented from using weapons, and required to show the kastij. ... If it is said: The Prophet did not take that from the Jews of Madinah nor the Christians of Najran nor the Magians of Hajar, so how can the dhimmi be required with this? We say: In the time of the Messenger of God, they were known in Madinah, their situation was not ambiguous, so there was no need for that. Then in the time of Umar, when among the people there were those known and unknown, the need arose, so he ordered that in the presence of the Companions, and they considered it correct. And because they are people of humiliation and Muslims are people of honor and dignity, distinction became obligatory to show the difference between them. And the kastij is the thick thread they tie around their waists. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a thick thread the size of a finger that the dhimmi ties over his clothes, unlike the silk belts that distinguish him. Fakhr al-Islam said: the kastijs are signs of disbelief, and it is an Arabicized Persian word, its real meaning being inability and humiliation in the Persian language.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses two main rulings in the chapter of Jizyah: (1) the maintenance and rebuilding of churches and synagogues in dar al-Islam, and (2) the requirement for dhimmis to be distinguished from Muslims in dress, riding, and other appearances. The text begins by stating that churches existing in Muslim territory may be maintained—if a church collapses on its own, it may be rebuilt, but not if the imam demolished it, and no increase over the original structure is allowed. This is the Hanafi position, supported by the practice since the Prophet's time of leaving churches and synagogues intact. Imam Ahmad holds that even rebuilding is not allowed. A distinction is made between cities (amṣār) and villages: in cities, where Islamic symbols are established, dhimmis are prevented from building new places of worship; in villages where Islamic rites are not performed, they may be allowed. In the Arabian Peninsula, they are prohibited from all such buildings due to the hadith 'Two religions shall not coexist in the Arabian Peninsula.' From Abu Hanifa, it is reported that he permitted churches in the villages of Kufa because most inhabitants were dhimmis. The second part requires dhimmis to be distinct from Muslims in dress (avoiding scholarly attire and Muslim headgear), mounts (not riding horses, but donkeys or mules with pack-saddles), and saddles (used only out of necessity, resembling pack-saddles). They must also display the kastij—a thick belt or thread tied over clothing as a sign of humiliation. The text answers an objection: why did the Prophet not impose such distinctions on the Jews of Madinah or Christians of Najran? Because in his time, they were well-known and no confusion arose. Later, when the Muslim community expanded and dhimmis became numerous, 'Umar instituted these measures with the Companions' consensus to maintain social distinction. The kastij is defined as a thick thread, about a finger's width, tied over the clothes, signifying the dhimmi's lowly status.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim protection (dhimma) who pays jizyah in exchange for security and religious freedom.
الكستيج (al-kastīj): A thick belt or thread worn over clothes by dhimmis as a distinguishing mark; it is a sign of humiliation.
الزي (al-zayy): Dress, appearance, or attire; here it refers to the distinct clothing imposed on dhimmis to mark their status.
التوارث (al-tawaruth): Continuous practice transmitted from generation to generation; here it refers to the practice of not demolishing churches since the Prophet's time, used as a proof for rebuilding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a dhimmi church that collapses naturally in a non-Arabian village?
A) It cannot be rebuilt at all.
B) It may be rebuilt but not beyond its original dimensions.
C) It may be rebuilt only with the imam's permission.
D) It may be rebuilt only if the Muslim population agrees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows maintenance of existing dhimmi places of worship but requires clear social distinction to preserve Islamic honor and prevent assimilation.

The Dispute on Presenting Islam to an Apostate
Commentary on apostates including definition, procedure, and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on presenting Islam to an apostate and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Core Idea
Presenting Islam is mustahabb, not wajib: the apostate's blood is forfeit without prior invitation.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the legal procedure for dealing with an apostate. The key point of contention between the Hanafi school and the majority is whether it is obligatory to invite the apostate back to Islam before executing him. We will examine the Hanafi proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and the thamarah al-khilaf in liability for pre-emptive killing.

Guided Path
1
Define apostasy and its conditions
Identify the linguistic and legal definition of al-murtadd, and list the conditions for valid apostasy according to the Hanafi school.
Conditions: reason, consciousness, voluntariness.
2
Locate the Hanafi procedure for an apostate
Note the three steps: presenting Islam (to remove doubts), imprisonment for three days, and execution if unrepentant.
The presentation is the disputed part.
3
Frame the inter-madhhab dispute
State the Hanafi view (mustahabb) and the opposing view (wajib) of Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali.
The Hanafi proof relies on absolute commands and the fact the call has already reached.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence: no liability (damān) in Hanafi if killed before presentation; potential liability in other schools.
This determines whether the killer must pay blood money.
5
Consider intra-Hanafi variation on repeated apostasy
Note the general view (accept repentance each time) and Abu Yusuf's view (kill without re-presentation if repeated).
The mufta bihi is the general view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المرتدين أي في بيان أحكامهم يعرض الإسلام على المرتد، وتكشف شبهته، ويحبس ثلاثة أيام، فإن أسلم، وإلا أي استحبابا عن الإسلام قتل وإسلامه أن يتبرأ عن الأديان سوى الإسلام، أي كيفية توبة المرتد فيها ونعمت باب المرتدين: لما فرغ من بيان أحكام الكفر الأصلي، شرع في بيان حكم الكفر العارضي. والمرتد لغة: الراجع، وشرعاً: الراجع عن دين الإسلام. وركن الردة: إجراء كلمة الكفر على اللسان بعد الإيمان، ويشترط لصحة الردة العقل والصحو والطوع، فلا تصح ردة مجنون ومعتوه وموسوس وصبي لا يعقل وسكران ومكره عليها، والبلوغ والذكورة ليسا بشرط. (فتح) العرض يعرض الإسلام على المرتد مطلقا سواء كان حراً أو عبداً رجلا أو امرأة، وعرض الإسلام عليه مستحب على الظاهر من المذهب على ما روي عن عمر الله، وليس بواجب؛ لأن الدعوة قد بلغته، غير أنه يحتمل أن اعتراه شبهة، فيعرض الإسلام عليه لتزول، ويعود إلى الإسلام، قال عليه لعلي انه "لئن يهدي الله بك رجلا واحدا خير أن تقتل ما بين المشرق والمغرب، إلا أن العرض غير واجب حتى لو قتله قاتل قبل عرض الإسلام لا يضمن من شيئاً، وقال الشافعي في قول ومالك وأحمد هو واجب رمز الحقائق ٤٤٢/١] (مستخلص، فتح) شبهته: أي شبهة المرتد التي وقعت في أمر دينه (ط عيني ويحبس ثلاثة أيام أي إذا أبى عن الإسلام بعد يحبس وجوباً، وقيل: ندباً ثلاثة أيام، يعرض عليه الإسلام في كل يوم إن استمهل هو للتأمل، فإن قيل: تقدير المدة بثلاثة أيام نصب للحكم بالرأي، أجيب بأن هذا من قبيل إثبات الحكم بدلالة النص؛ في خيار البيع بثلاثة أيام لأن ورود النص فيه؛ لأن التقدير بثلاثة أيام هناك إنما كان للتأمل، وقيل: يستحب الإمهال مطلقاً . استمهل أولا للتأمل وكشف الشبهة. وقال الشافعي: الإمهال ،واجب لا يحل للإمام أن يقتله قبل أن يمضي عليه ثلاثة أيام؛ لأن ارتداد المسلم لا يكون إلا عن الشبهة ظاهرا فلابد من مدة للتأمل، ولنا: إطلاق النصوص كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: ٥) من غير الإمهال وقوله علية: "من بدل دينه فاقتلوه"؛ ولأنه كافر حربي، بلغته الدعوة، فلا يجوز تأخير قتله لأجل الموهوم، ولا فرق فيه بين الحر والعبد، فإن ارتد وتاب ثم ارتد، تقبل توبته، وهكذا دائماً، وعن أبي يوسف: إذا تكرر منه الارتداد يقتل من غير عرض الإسلام عليه؛ لأنه مستخف بالدين. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/١] مستخلص فتح وإلا قتل [ أي وإن لم يسلم في ثلاثة أيام. (عيني)] لقوله عليه: "من بدل دينه فاقتلوه"، رواه البخاري وأحمد، ويلقي في حفرة كالكلب. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/١] وإسلامه إلخ: قيد بإسلام المرتد ؛ لأن الكفار أصناف خمسة: الأول: من ينكر الصانع كالدهرية. والثاني: من ينكر الوحدانية كالثنوية. والثالث: من يقر بهما لكن ينكر بعثة الرسل كالفلاسفة والرابع من ينكر الكل كالوثنية.
Chapter on apostates: That is, an explanation of their rulings. He presents Islam to the apostate, and his doubt is removed, and he is imprisoned for three days. If he accepts Islam (then fine), otherwise he is killed. And his acceptance of Islam is that he disavows all religions besides Islam, that is, the manner of the apostate's repentance. The chapter on apostates: When he finished explaining the rulings of original disbelief, he began to explain the ruling of temporary disbelief. Al-Murtadd linguistically: the one who returns; legally: the one who returns from the religion of Islam. The pillar of apostasy is uttering a word of disbelief with the tongue after faith. For the validity of apostasy, reason, consciousness, and voluntariness are conditions; so the apostasy of a madman, an imbecile, a waswas, a child without intellect, a drunkard, and one coerced is not valid. Puberty and masculinity are not conditions. (Fath) The presentation: He presents Islam to the apostate absolutely, whether free or slave, man or woman. Presenting Islam to him is recommended (mustahabb) according to the apparent position of the school, as narrated from Umar (RA), and it is not obligatory; because the call has already reached him. However, it is possible that a doubt has overtaken him, so Islam is presented to him so that it might disappear and he returns to Islam. The Prophet (PBUH) said: 'If Allah guides one man through you, it is better for you than everything between the east and the west.' However, the presentation is not obligatory, even if someone kills him before presenting Islam, he is not liable for anything. Al-Shafi'i in one opinion, and Malik and Ahmad hold it is obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/442] (Mustakhlas, Fath) His doubt: that is, the apostate's doubt that occurred concerning his religion. (Ayni) And he is imprisoned for three days: i.e., if he refuses Islam, he is imprisoned obligatorily, and it is said: recommendatorily, for three days, and he is presented Islam every day if he asks for respite for reflection. If it is said: estimating the period as three days is establishing a ruling by opinion, it is answered: this is from the category of establishing a ruling by indication of the text, as in the option of sale for three days because the text exists for it; for the estimation of three days there was for reflection. And it is said: giving respite is recommended absolutely, whether he asked for it at first or not, for reflection and removing doubt. Al-Shafi'i said: Giving respite is obligatory; it is not permissible for the imam to kill him before three days have passed, because the apostasy of a Muslim only occurs from doubt apparently, so a period for reflection is necessary. Our proof: the absoluteness of the texts such as His saying: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' (al-Tawbah 9:5) without respite, and his saying: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' And because he is a harbi disbeliever, the call has reached him, so it is not permissible to delay his killing for the sake of a doubt. There is no difference between free and slave. If he apostatizes and repents then apostatizes again, his repentance is accepted, and so on perpetually. According to Abu Yusuf: If apostasy is repeated from him, he is killed without presenting Islam to him, because he is mocking religion. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/442] (Mustakhlas, Fath) And if not [he accepts Islam], he is killed [i.e., if he does not accept Islam in three days (Ayni)] by his saying: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him,' narrated by Bukhari and Ahmad. And he is thrown into a pit like a dog. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/442] And his Islam etc.: He restricted it to the apostate's acceptance of Islam because the disbelievers are of five kinds: first: those who deny the Creator, like the Dahriyya. Second: those who deny Oneness, like the Dualists. Third: those who affirm both but deny the sending of messengers, like the philosophers. Fourth: those who deny all, like the idolaters.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary on the chapter of apostates (Bab al-Murtaddin). It first defines apostasy (riddah) linguistically and legally, and states its pillar (rukn): uttering a word of disbelief after having faith. Conditions for valid apostasy are reason, consciousness, and voluntariness; thus the apostasy of the insane, intoxicated, or coerced is invalid. Minors and women can apostatize validly (puberty and masculinity not required). The procedure: The apostate is called to Islam and his doubts are removed. Presenting Islam is mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not wajib, because the call has already reached him. The text cites a hadith about the superiority of guiding one man. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools (according to one view) hold it is wajib. The Hanafi proof is the general Quranic command 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' and the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him'—both without requiring prior invitation. The apostate is imprisoned for three days, with a dispute on whether this is wajib or nadb. The period is based on the analogy of the three-day option in sales (khiyar al-shart), which is established by textual indication. The Hanafi response to objections is that the three-day period is not arbitrary but derived from established precedent. If the apostate repents multiple times, repentance is accepted each time according to the general principle; but Abu Yusuf holds that if it recurs, he should be killed without further invitation because it shows contempt for religion. The passage ends with a categorization of disbelievers: deniers of the Creator, deniers of Oneness, deniers of prophethood, and total deniers.

Key Terms
المرتد (al-murtadd): The one who returns from Islam to disbelief by word or deed after being a Muslim.
الردة (al-riddah): The act of apostasy, whose pillar is uttering a word of disbelief after faith.
عرض الإسلام (ard al-Islam): Presenting Islam to the apostate and inviting him to return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on presenting Islam to an apostate before execution?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the absolute command to kill the apostate over the recommendation to invite him, making presentation mustahabb—a key difference from the majority.

Procedure for the Apostate: Presentation, Imprisonment, and Execution
Inter-madhhab dispute on obligations before executing an apostate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on presenting Islam to an apostate and imprisonment before execution, and explain why the Hanafi school considers presentation mustahabb not wajib, contrasting with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Hanafi: presentation is recommended, not required; execution after three days is wajib if unrepentant.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the treatment of an apostate before execution. While the Shafi‘i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools consider it obligatory to present Islam and grant a three-day respite, the Hanafi school adopts a different approach based on its reading of the primary texts. Understanding this difference reveals how usul principles shape furu‘ rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on presentation
Identify that the Hanafi school holds presentation of Islam to be mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. Confirm the basis: the da‘wa has already reached the apostate.
2
Contrast with the opposing school
Note that al-Shafi‘i (in one view), Malik, and Ahmad consider presentation wajib. Their reasoning: apostasy arises from doubt, so a delay is needed for reflection.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
Examine the Hanafi dalil: absolute verses (e.g., Q.9:5) and the hadith 'Man baddala dinahu faqtuluh', which do not mandate delay. The apostate is a harbi who has been reached by the call.
Also note the intra-Hanafi difference from Abu Yusuf regarding repeated apostasy.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: if an apostate is killed before presentation, the Hanafi school holds no liability (diya/kaffarah), while the Shafi‘i school may impose liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعرض الإسلام على المرتد مطلقا سواء كان حراً أو عبداً رجلا أو امرأة، وعرض الإسلام عليه مستحب على الظاهر من المذهب على ما روي عن عمر الله، وليس بواجب؛ لأن الدعوة قد بلغته، غير أنه يحتمل أن اعتراه شبهة، فيعرض الإسلام عليه لتزول، ويعود إلى الإسلام، قال عليه لعلي انه "لئن يهدي الله بك رجلا واحدا خير أن تقتل ما بين المشرق والمغرب، إلا أن العرض غير واجب حتى لو قتله قاتل قبل عرض الإسلام لا يضمن من شيئاً، وقال الشافعي في قول ومالك وأحمد هو واجب رمز الحقائق ٤٤٢/١] (مستخلص، فتح) شبهته: أي شبهة المرتد التي وقعت في أمر دينه (ط عيني ويحبس ثلاثة أيام أي إذا أبى عن الإسلام بعد يحبس وجوباً، وقيل: ندباً ثلاثة أيام، يعرض عليه الإسلام في كل يوم إن استمهل هو للتأمل، فإن قيل: تقدير المدة بثلاثة أيام نصب للحكم بالرأي، أجيب بأن هذا من قبيل إثبات الحكم بدلالة النص؛ في خيار البيع بثلاثة أيام لأن ورود النص فيه؛ لأن التقدير بثلاثة أيام هناك إنما كان للتأمل، وقيل: يستحب الإمهال مطلقاً . استمهل أولا للتأمل وكشف الشبهة. وقال الشافعي: الإمهال ،واجب لا يحل للإمام أن يقتله قبل أن يمضي عليه ثلاثة أيام؛ لأن ارتداد المسلم لا يكون إلا عن الشبهة ظاهرا فلابد من مدة للتأمل، ولنا: إطلاق النصوص كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: ٥) من غير الإمهال وقوله علية: "من بدل دينه فاقتلوه"؛ ولأنه كافر حربي، بلغته الدعوة، فلا يجوز تأخير قتله لأجل الموهوم، ولا فرق فيه بين الحر والعبد، فإن ارتد وتاب ثم ارتد، تقبل توبته، وهكذا دائماً، وعن أبي يوسف: إذا تكرر منه الارتداد يقتل من غير عرض الإسلام عليه؛ لأنه مستخف بالدين. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/١] مستخلص فتح وإلا قتل [ أي وإن لم يسلم في ثلاثة أيام. (عيني)] لقوله عليه: "من بدل دينه فاقتلوه"، رواه البخاري وأحمد، ويلقي في حفرة كالكلب. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/١]
Islam is presented to the apostate absolutely, whether he is free or a slave, male or female. Presenting Islam to him is recommended (mustahabb) in the apparent position of the school, as related from ‘Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and it is not obligatory, because the call has already reached him. However, it is possible that a doubt has occurred to him, so Islam is presented to him to remove it and he may return to Islam. He (peace be upon him) said: 'If Allah guides a single man through you, that is better for you than whatever is between the east and west.' Yet presentation is not obligatory, so if someone kills him before presenting Islam, he is not liable for anything. Al-Shafi‘i, in one opinion, and Malik and Ahmad said it is obligatory. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/442] (Mukhtasar, Fath) His doubt: i.e., the doubt of the apostate that occurred concerning his religion. (Tah, ‘Ayni) And he is imprisoned for three days: i.e., if he refuses Islam after [presentation], he is imprisoned obligatorily, and it is said: recommendably, for three days. Islam is presented to him each day if he asks for a delay to reflect. For if it is said: specifying the period as three days is a ruling based on opinion, it is answered that this is a case of establishing a ruling by implication of the text, as in the option of purchase for three days because the text is found there; the specification of three days there was for reflection. And it is said: granting respite is recommended absolutely, whether he first asks for a delay to reflect and remove the doubt. Al-Shafi‘i said: granting respite is obligatory; it is not permissible for the imam to kill him before three days have passed, because a Muslim's apostasy only occurs due to apparent doubt, so a period for reflection is necessary. Our evidence: the absolute texts, such as Allah's saying: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' (al-Tawbah 5) without requiring respite, and his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him.' And because he is a warring disbeliever (harbi) whom the call has reached, so it is not permissible to delay his killing because of a hypothetical matter. There is no difference in this between the free and the slave. If he apostatizes and then repents and apostatizes again, his repentance is accepted, and so on always. From Abu Yusuf: if apostasy is repeated from him, he is killed without presenting Islam to him, because he is mocking the religion. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/442] Mukhtasar Fath. And if not, he is killed: i.e., if he does not accept Islam within three days. (al-‘Ayni) Due to his saying: 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him,' narrated by Bukhari and Ahmad. And he is thrown into a pit like a dog. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/442]
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and a ruling statement. It explains the Hanafi procedure for dealing with an apostate. First, Islam is presented to him unconditionally—whether free or slave, male or female. The presentation is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, because the da‘wa has already reached him. The basis for recommendation is the hadith about guiding one man. However, presentation is not wajib; if someone kills the apostate before presentation, there is no diya or kaffarah. The Shafi‘is, Malik, and Ahmad (in one view) consider it wajib. Then the apostate is imprisoned for three days. There are two opinions: obligatory or recommended. During imprisonment, Islam is presented each day if he requests time to reflect. The three-day period is derived by analogy from khiyar al-bay‘ (option in sale) which is based on nas. Al-Shafi‘i holds that three days are obligatory for reflection. The Hanafi response cites absolute verses and hadiths that do not require delay, as the apostate is a harbi and the call has reached him. There is no difference between free and slave. If the apostate repents and then apostatizes repeatedly, his repentance is always accepted, except according to Abu Yusuf, who says if repetition indicates mockery, he is killed without presentation. If he does not accept Islam within three days, he is killed based on the hadith, and his body is disposed of in a pit.

Key Terms
العرض (al-‘ard): Presenting Islam to the apostate and inviting him to repent.
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment of the apostate for three days to allow reflection.
الإمهال (al-imhal): Respite/granting time to the apostate before execution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on presenting Islam to an apostate before execution?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the absolute command to execute the apostate, considering presentation as recommended but not essential, while the Shafi‘i school emphasizes the need for reflection before punishment.

Repentance of the Apostate: What Constitutes Islam
Explains what an apostate must say to repent, referencing five types of disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for an apostate's repentance and identify which verbal or action-based deeds constitute acceptance of Islam according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The apostate's repentance requires disavowal of all false religions; the required declaration varies by type of disbelief, and certain actions also effect Islam.

Becoming Muslim after apostasy is a serious matter — it must be unambiguous. The Hanafi school details what exactly an apostate must say or do to validly return to Islam, tailored to the specific form of disbelief they had adopted. This lesson unpacks the five categories of disbelievers and the corresponding sufficiencies for repentance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is the apostate's repentance (tawba) and acceptance of Islam. It is an act of 'ibada that nullifies previous disbelief.
The ruling is about validity (sihha) of the repentance, not obligation.
2
Classify the disbeliever into one of five types
The passage divides kuffār into five categories based on what they deny: Creator, Tawhid, Prophethood, all, or universal prophethood of Muhammad.
This classification determines which formula suffices.
3
Determine the sufficient verbal formula for the type
For each type, a specific part of the shahada (or both plus disavowal) is enough.
Memorize: types 1-2 need only 'La ilaha illa Allah'; type 3 needs 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'; type 4 needs either; type 5 needs both plus tabarrī.
4
Recognize that actions can also constitute Islam
Besides verbal declaration, certain actions (e.g., praying an obligatory prayer behind an imam, calling adhan, sajda tilawa, paying zakat on grazing livestock) suffice to signify acceptance of Islam.
Not all actions qualify — charity alone is not enough.
5
Note the condition of knowledge
The repenter must know that the words or actions represent Islam, and knowledge of the Prophet's name (Muhammad) is sufficient — knowledge of his lineage is not required.
This prevents invalidity due to ignorance of details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإسلامه أن يتبرأ عن الأديان سوى الإسلام، أي كيفية توبة المرتد سوى دين الإسلام فيها ونعمت . وإسلامه إلخ: قيد بإسلام المرتد ؛ لأن الكفار أصناف خمسة: الأول: من ينكر الصانع كالدهرية. والثاني: من ينكر الوحدانية كالثنوية. والثالث: من يقر بهما لكن ينكر بعثة الرسل كالفلاسفة والرابع من ينكر الكل كالوثنية. والخامس من يقر بالكل، لكن ينكر عموم رسالة المصطفى الله كالعيسوية. فيكفى في الأولين بقول لا إله إلا الله، وفي الثالث: بقول محمد رسول الله، وفي الرابع بأحدهما، وفي الخامس بهما مع التبري عن كل دين يخالف دين الإسلام وإنما كانت توبة المرتد بالتبري عن الأديان كلها غير دين الإسلام؛ لأنه لا دین حتى يكلف بالتبري عنه، وفيه إشعار بأنه لو قال الكافر: "لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله" يصير مسلماً إذا علم أنه الإسلام، ويشترط معرفة اسمه عليها دون معرفة اسم أبيه وجده ثم اعلم أن الإسلام كما يكون بالقول يكون بالفعل أيضاً كما لو صلى مكتوبة وأتمها مقتدياً أو أذن في الوقت، أو سجد للتلاوة، أو أدى زكاة السائمة لا بغير ذلك.(فتح) أو عما انتقل إليه :: أي أو يتبرأ عن الدين الذي انتقل. (مص) إليه؛ لحصول المقصود، والأول هو الأولى؛ لأن المرتد لا دین له. (عيني)
And his accepting Islam (Islamuhu) is that he disavows all religions except Islam. That is the manner of the apostate's repentance, i.e., excluding the religion of Islam, and it is good. 'And his accepting Islam' etc.: It is restricted to the apostate's becoming Muslim because the disbelievers are of five types: the first: one who denies the Creator, like the Dahriyya. The second: one who denies Oneness, like the Dualists. The third: one who affirms both but denies the sending of messengers, like the philosophers. The fourth: one who denies all, like the polytheists. The fifth: one who affirms all but denies the universality of the mission of the Chosen One (peace be upon him), like the ‘Isawiyya. For the first two, the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' suffices; for the third, the statement 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'; for the fourth, either of the two; for the fifth, both along with disavowal of every religion that opposes the religion of Islam. The apostate's repentance is by disavowing all religions other than the religion of Islam because he has no religion such that he would be required to disavow it. And this implies that if a disbeliever says: 'La ilaha illa Allah Muhammadun Rasul Allah', he becomes Muslim if he knows that this is Islam. Knowledge of the Prophet's name is required, not knowledge of his father's and grandfather's name. Then know that Islam occurs by action as well as speech, such as if he prays an obligatory prayer and completes it following an imam, or calls the adhan at the right time, or prostrates for tilawa, or pays zakat on grazing livestock—not by other than that. (Fath) 'Or from that which he transferred to': i.e., or he disavows the religion to which he transferred. (Mughrib) to achieve the purpose, and the first is better because the apostate has no religion. (al-‘Ayni)
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the repentance of an apostate. It explains that his acceptance of Islam (Islamuhu) is by disavowing all religions except Islam. The author details that disbelievers are divided into five categories: (1) those who deny the Creator (e.g., Dahriyya/atheists), (2) those who deny monotheism (e.g., Dualists), (3) those who affirm Creator and Tawhid but deny prophethood (e.g., philosophers), (4) those who deny all (polytheists), and (5) those who affirm all but deny the universal prophethood of Muhammad (e.g., a Jewish sect?). For the first two, saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' suffices; for the third, saying 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'; for the fourth, either one; for the fifth, both plus disavowal of all other religions. The apostate must disavow all other religions because he currently has no valid religion to disavow. The text also implies that if a disbeliever says the shahada knowingly, he becomes Muslim, and it is enough to know the name of the Prophet (not his lineage). Additionally, Islam can be accepted by actions: performing salah completely behind an imam, giving adhan, sajda tilawa, or paying zakat on grazing livestock, but not by other actions. The commentary of al-‘Ayni notes that it is better to disavow the religion he adopted because he has no religion.

Key Terms
التبري (al-tabarrī): Disavowal or renunciation of false religions.
أصناف الكفار (asnāf al-kuffār): Five categories of disbelievers based on what they deny.
المرتد (al-murtadd): Apostate; a Muslim who leaves Islam.
التوبة (al-tawba): Repentance; return to Islam after apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions does NOT constitute acceptance of Islam?
A) Praying a full obligatory prayer behind an imam
B) Reciting the adhan at the correct time
C) Giving charity to a poor person
D) Performing sajda al-tilawa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides specific verbal and action-based paths for an apostate to validly return to Islam, depending on the type of disbelief they had adopted.
